Fleetwood passed away on November 9 or 10, 2015.[[112]](#cite_note-fleetwood-112) The film was also made available for viewing by astronauts on the [International Space Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Space_Station "wikipedia:International Space Station").[[113]](#cite_note-113) On November 28, it was revealed that [R2-KT](/wiki/R2-KT "R2-KT"), the droid built in honor of [Katie Johnson](/wiki/Katie_Johnson "Katie Johnson"), would make an appearance in *The Force Awakens*.[[114]](#cite_note-R2KT-TFA-114) [Albin Johnson](/wiki/Albin_Johnson "Albin Johnson"), founder of the [501st Legion](/wiki/501st_Legion_(fan_organization) "501st Legion (fan organization)") and father of Katie, had constructed the droid after she was diagnosed with terminal brain cancer. In addition to R2-KT's appearance, a variation of the 501st's logo was featured as a flag outside Maz Kanata's castle.[[115]](#cite_note-501FB-115)

## Adaptations and tie-in media[]

 [![Teaser poster from the D23 Expo](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIABAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAEALAAAAAABAAEAQAICTAEAOw%3D%3D)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/14/SWTheForceAwakensStruzanD23Poster.png/revision/latest?cb=20171022074511) [![Teaser poster from the D23 Expo](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/14/SWTheForceAwakensStruzanD23Poster.png/revision/latest/scale-to-width-down/180?cb=20171022074511)](https://static.wikia.nocookie.net/starwars/images/1/14/SWTheForceAwakensStruzanD23Poster.png/revision/latest?cb=20171022074511) 

Teaser poster from the D23 Expo

 

Following Disney's acquisition of Lucasfilm in 2012, its "[imagineers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Disney_Imagineering "wikipedia:Walt Disney Imagineering")" began developing *Star Wars*–themed expansions to the various Disney theme parks. However, Bob Iger halted work on these expansions until *The Force Awakens* and other future *Star Wars* films had reached a point in their development that elements from those projects could be included.[[6]](#cite_note-Theme-6) On [August 15](/wiki/August_15 "August 15"), 2015, it was announced that plans were moving forward for a *Star Wars*-themed section of the Disney parks, which would include content based on *The Force Awakens*.[[116]](#cite_note-SW-New_and_Enhanced_Star_Wars_Experiences_Coming_to_Disney_Parks-116)

Disney's merchandising campaign for the film began on [September 4](/wiki/September_4 "September 4"), 2015—dubbed "[Force Friday](/wiki/Force_Friday "Force Friday")."[[117]](#cite_note-SW-Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens_Products_to_Arrive_on_'Force_Friday,'_September_4-117) Lucasfilm has published a [series of books and comics](/wiki/Journey_to_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens "Journey to Star Wars: The Force Awakens") that connect *Return of the Jedi* and *The Force Awakens*.[[118]](#cite_note-SW-Journey_to_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens_Publishing_Program_Coming_Fall_2015-118)[[119]](#cite_note-JourneyAnnounce-119) A [novelization](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens_(novelization) "Star Wars: The Force Awakens (novelization)") was released,[[120]](#cite_note-novelization-120) as well as a number of other titles directly connected to the film, such as an [art book](/wiki/The_Art_of_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens "The Art of Star Wars: The Force Awakens"),[[121]](#cite_note-Amazon-121) a [character anthology](/wiki/Before_the_Awakening "Before the Awakening"),[[122]](#cite_note-awakensanthology-122) and [*Ultimate Sticker Collection*](/wiki/Ultimate_Sticker_Collection:_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens "Ultimate Sticker Collection: Star Wars: The Force Awakens").[[123]](#cite_note-ultimatesticker-123) Content from *The Force Awakens* was also featured in the video games *[Disney Infinity 3.0](/wiki/Disney_Infinity_3.0 "Disney Infinity 3.0")*, *[Star Wars Battlefront](/wiki/Star_Wars_Battlefront "Star Wars Battlefront")* and *[LEGO Star Wars: The Force Awakens](/wiki/LEGO_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens "LEGO Star Wars: The Force Awakens")*.[[124]](#cite_note-SW-Star_Wars_Comes_to_Disney_Infinity_3.0!-124)[[125]](#cite_note-SW-EA_Previews_the_Battle_of_Jakku_on_Star_Wars_Battlefront!-125)[[126]](#cite_note-SW-Calling_All_Jedi_Masters_and_Master_Builders:_Announcing_LEGO_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens-126) The company partnered with eight major brands: Covergirl & Max Factor, Duracell, FCA US, General Mills, HP, Subway, and Verizon.[[127]](#cite_note-grip-127) Beginning in August 2015, [Target](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Target_Corporation "wikipedia:Target Corporation") stores held a campaign called "Share the Force," which included TV ads, exclusive in-store merchandise, and an online program in which *Star Wars* fans could submit images and videos that captured their memories of the franchise.[[128]](#cite_note-128) Some of Japan's [All Nippon Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All_Nippon_Airways "wikipedia:All Nippon Airways") airplanes were painted to reflect elements from *The Force Awakens*.[[129]](#cite_note-129)

The merchandise garnered criticism as it lacked Rey's presence: [Hasbro](/wiki/Hasbro "Hasbro") announced it would re-release its *Force Awakens* Monopoly set to include her after it excluded her in favor of Darth Vader, who is not in the movie. Abrams said he was not involved much in the merchandising, and that when "I read that she wasn't in the Monopoly game and was quickly making phone calls about this because if it were true — and it is true, and now Hasbro, of course, has said they're going to put Rey in — it doesn't quite make sense why she wouldn't be there."[[130]](#cite_note-130)

### Home media[]

*The Force Awakens* was released in a Blu-ray combo pack and on DVD on [April 5](/wiki/April_5 "April 5"), [2016](/wiki/2016 "2016"), with a digital version available four days earlier on [April 1](/wiki/April_1 "April 1"). Special features included deleted scenes, featurettes, and a feature-length documentary, *[Secrets of The Force Awakens: A Cinematic Journey](/wiki/Secrets_of_The_Force_Awakens:_A_Cinematic_Journey "Secrets of The Force Awakens: A Cinematic Journey")*. Various retailers also included exclusive content and/or packaging,[[131]](#cite_note-TFA_Digital_HD-131) and one deleted scene was exclusive to the digital download.[[132]](#cite_note-132) On [March 23](/wiki/March_23 "March 23"), 2016, the film was leaked online prior to its original Blu-ray release and was downloaded more than two million times in twelve hours.[[133]](#cite_note-133) A 3D Collector's Edition was also released in late 2016, containing Blu-ray 3D, Blu-ray, Digital HD and DVD versions of the film. It included all of the bonus features from the original release, as well as an audio commentary by J.J. Abrams, additional deleted scenes, and additional behind-the-scenes conversations with cast and crew.[[134]](#cite_note-3D-134)

The film made its television debut on the [Starz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Starz "wikipedia:Starz") channels, beginning September 10, 2016.[[135]](#cite_note-135)

## Reception ‡[]

Theater tickets became available for pre-order on October 19th,[[88]](#cite_note-Poster-88) with many online retailers experiencing outages due to heavy demand, including top sites such as [Fandango](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fandango_(ticket_service) "wikipedia:Fandango (ticket service)").[[136]](#cite_note-136)[[137]](#cite_note-137) By the time of the film's release, over $100 million in pre-release tickets were sold, bypassing the previous record, held by [*The Dark Knight*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film) "wikipedia:The Dark Knight (film)").[[138]](#cite_note-138)

On January 6, 2016, the film broke the record for the highest box-office gross for a film in the United States, beating the previous record of $760.5 million held by the 2009 epic science-fiction film [*Avatar*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film) "wikipedia:Avatar (2009 film)") by James Cameron. The record was reached less than three weeks after release.[[139]](#cite_note-boxofficerecord-139) Adjusted for ticket price inflation, *The Force Awakens* is the most successful sequel of all time, narrowly beating *Star Wars*: Episode V *The Empire Strikes Back*.[[140]](#cite_note-Box_Office_Mojo_All_Time_Adjusted-140) On [February 7](/wiki/February_7 "February 7"), 2016, the film was reported to have crossed the threshold of $2 billion in ticket sales.[[141]](#cite_note-ewbillions-141)

*The Force Awakens* was nominated for five Oscars at the 88th Academy Awards (the largest number of award nominations for a single *Star Wars* film since *A New Hope*), held on [February 28](/wiki/February_28 "February 28"), 2016. The film was nominated in the categories of Best Film Editing for [Maryann Brandon](/wiki/Maryann_Brandon "Maryann Brandon") and [Mary Jo Markey](/wiki/Mary_Jo_Markey "Mary Jo Markey"); Best Original Score for John Williams; Best Sound Editing for Matthew Wood and David Acord; Best Sound Mixing for Andy Nelson, Christopher Scarabosio, and Stuart Wilson; and Best Visual Effects for Roger Guyett, Patrick Tubach, Neal Scanlan, and Chris Corbould.[[142]](#cite_note-Oscar_Noms-142) The general public voted *The Force Awakens* Movie of the Year at the [2016 MTV Movie Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_MTV_Movie_Awards "wikipedia:2016 MTV Movie Awards"); Daisy Ridley was also voted Best Breakthrough Performance, while Adam Driver won Best Villain.[[143]](#cite_note-143)

According to Robert Iger's 2019 memoir *The Ride of a Lifetime*, George Lucas was not pleased with the film, feeling that it lacked creativity or innovation. On his part, Iger explained that his company intended to make a film that was familiar to what had come before.[[144]](#cite_note-144) Kathleen Kennedy later commented on this to *Rolling Stone*: "He may not agree with every choice J.J. made. He may not agree with every choice Rian made. But he appreciates the film-making. That I know."[[145]](#cite_note-145)

Abrams admitted one problem with the film, namely Rey and Leia hugging at the end, although it is not established that they know each other. Abrams explained Chewbacca was preoccupied with getting Finn medical attention, while Rey and Leia had spoken via transmitter off screen. He said, "Had Chewbacca not been where he was, you probably wouldn't have thought of it. But because he was right there, passed by Leia, it felt almost like a slight, which was definitely not the intention."[[146]](#cite_note-146)
